    2057                 :          2 : }
    2058                 :            : 
    2059                 :            : /*
    2060                 :            :  * ==========================================================================
    2061                 :            :  * Gang blocks.
    2062                 :            :  *
    2063                 :            :  * A gang block is a collection of small blocks that looks to the DMU
    2064                 :            :  * like one large block.  When zio_dva_allocate() cannot find a block
    2065                 :            :  * of the requested size, due to either severe fragmentation or the pool
    2066                 :            :  * being nearly full, it calls zio_write_gang_block() to construct the
    2067                 :            :  * block from smaller fragments.
    2068                 :            :  *
    2069                 :            :  * A gang block consists of a gang header (zio_gbh_phys_t) and up to
    2070                 :            :  * three (SPA_GBH_NBLKPTRS) gang members.  The gang header is just like
    2071                 :            :  * an indirect block: it's an array of block pointers.  It consumes
    2072                 :            :  * only one sector and hence is allocatable regardless of fragmentation.
    2073                 :            :  * The gang header's bps point to its gang members, which hold the data.
    2074                 :            :  *
    2075                 :            :  * Gang blocks are self-checksumming, using the bp's <vdev, offset, txg>
    2076                 :            :  * as the verifier to ensure uniqueness of the SHA256 checksum.
    2077                 :            :  * Critically, the gang block bp's blk_cksum is the checksum of the data,
    2078                 :            :  * not the gang header.  This ensures that data block signatures (needed for
    2079                 :            :  * deduplication) are independent of how the block is physically stored.
    2080                 :            :  *
    2081                 :            :  * Gang blocks can be nested: a gang member may itself be a gang block.
    2082                 :            :  * Thus every gang block is a tree in which root and all interior nodes are
    2083                 :            :  * gang headers, and the leaves are normal blocks that contain user data.
    2084                 :            :  * The root of the gang tree is called the gang leader.
    2085                 :            :  *
    2086                 :            :  * To perform any operation (read, rewrite, free, claim) on a gang block,
    2087                 :            :  * zio_gang_assemble() first assembles the gang tree (minus data leaves)
    2088                 :            :  * in the io_gang_tree field of the original logical i/o by recursively
    2089                 :            :  * reading the gang leader and all gang headers below it.  This yields
    2090                 :            :  * an in-core tree containing the contents of every gang header and the
    2091                 :            :  * bps for every constituent of the gang block.
    2092                 :            :  *
    2093                 :            :  * With the gang tree now assembled, zio_gang_issue() just walks the gang tree
    2094                 :            :  * and invokes a callback on each bp.  To free a gang block, zio_gang_issue()
    2095                 :            :  * calls zio_free_gang() -- a trivial wrapper around zio_free() -- for each bp.
    2096                 :            :  * zio_claim_gang() provides a similarly trivial wrapper for zio_claim().
    2097                 :            :  * zio_read_gang() is a wrapper around zio_read() that omits reading gang
    2098                 :            :  * headers, since we already have those in io_gang_tree.  zio_rewrite_gang()
    2099                 :            :  * performs a zio_rewrite() of the data or, for gang headers, a zio_rewrite()
    2100                 :            :  * of the gang header plus zio_checksum_compute() of the data to update the
    2101                 :            :  * gang header's blk_cksum as described above.
    2102                 :            :  *
    2103                 :            :  * The two-phase assemble/issue model solves the problem of partial failure --
    2104                 :            :  * what if you'd freed part of a gang block but then couldn't read the
    2105                 :            :  * gang header for another part?  Assembling the entire gang tree first
    2106                 :            :  * ensures that all the necessary gang header I/O has succeeded before
    2107                 :            :  * starting the actual work of free, claim, or write.  Once the gang tree
    2108                 :            :  * is assembled, free and claim are in-memory operations that cannot fail.
    2109                 :            :  *
    2110                 :            :  * In the event that a gang write fails, zio_dva_unallocate() walks the
    2111                 :            :  * gang tree to immediately free (i.e. insert back into the space map)
    2112                 :            :  * everything we've allocated.  This ensures that we don't get ENOSPC
    2113                 :            :  * errors during repeated suspend/resume cycles due to a flaky device.
    2114                 :            :  *
    2115                 :            :  * Gang rewrites only happen during sync-to-convergence.  If we can't assemble
    2116                 :            :  * the gang tree, we won't modify the block, so we can safely defer the free
    2117                 :            :  * (knowing that the block is still intact).  If we *can* assemble the gang
    2118                 :            :  * tree, then even if some of the rewrites fail, zio_dva_unallocate() will free
    2119                 :            :  * each constituent bp and we can allocate a new block on the next sync pass.
    2120                 :            :  *
    2121                 :            :  * In all cases, the gang tree allows complete recovery from partial failure.
    2122                 :            :  * ==========================================================================
    2123                 :            :  */
    2124                 :            : 
    2125                 :            : static void
    2126                 :      28391 : zio_gang_issue_func_done(zio_t *zio)
    2127                 :            : {
    2128                 :      28391 :         abd_put(zio->io_abd);
    2129                 :      28396 : }

    2567                 :            : 
    2568                 :            : /*
    2569                 :            :  * The zio_nop_write stage in the pipeline determines if allocating a
    2570                 :            :  * new bp is necessary.  The nopwrite feature can handle writes in
    2571                 :            :  * either syncing or open context (i.e. zil writes) and as a result is
    2572                 :            :  * mutually exclusive with dedup.
    2573                 :            :  *
    2574                 :            :  * By leveraging a cryptographically secure checksum, such as SHA256, we
    2575                 :            :  * can compare the checksums of the new data and the old to determine if
    2576                 :            :  * allocating a new block is required.  Note that our requirements for
    2577                 :            :  * cryptographic strength are fairly weak: there can't be any accidental
    2578                 :            :  * hash collisions, but we don't need to be secure against intentional
    2579                 :            :  * (malicious) collisions.  To trigger a nopwrite, you have to be able
    2580                 :            :  * to write the file to begin with, and triggering an incorrect (hash
    2581                 :            :  * collision) nopwrite is no worse than simply writing to the file.
    2582                 :            :  * That said, there are no known attacks against the checksum algorithms
    2583                 :            :  * used for nopwrite, assuming that the salt and the checksums
    2584                 :            :  * themselves remain secret.
    2585                 :            :  */
    2586                 :            : static int
    2587                 :       4666 : zio_nop_write(zio_t *zio)
    2588                 :            : {
    2589                 :       4666 :         blkptr_t *bp = zio->io_bp;
    2590                 :       4666 :         blkptr_t *bp_orig = &zio->io_bp_orig;
    2591                 :       4666 :         zio_prop_t *zp = &zio->io_prop;
    2592                 :            : 
    2593         [ -  + ]:       4666 :         ASSERT(BP_GET_LEVEL(bp) == 0);
    2594         [ -  + ]:       4666 :         ASSERT(!(zio->io_flags & ZIO_FLAG_IO_REWRITE));
    2595         [ -  + ]:       4666 :         ASSERT(zp->zp_nopwrite);
    2596         [ -  + ]:       4666 :         ASSERT(!zp->zp_dedup);
    2597         [ -  + ]:       4666 :         ASSERT(zio->io_bp_override == NULL);
    2598         [ -  + ]:       4666 :         ASSERT(IO_IS_ALLOCATING(zio));
    2599                 :            : 
    2600                 :            :         /*

    4381                 :            :  * This is simple in every case aside from the meta-dnode object. For all other
    4382                 :            :  * objects, we traverse them in order (object 1 before object 2, and so on).
    4383                 :            :  * However, all of these objects are traversed while traversing object 0, since
    4384                 :            :  * the data it points to is the list of objects.  Thus, we need to convert to a
    4385                 :            :  * canonical representation so we can compare meta-dnode bookmarks to
    4386                 :            :  * non-meta-dnode bookmarks.
    4387                 :            :  *
    4388                 :            :  * We do this by calculating "equivalents" for each field of the zbookmark.
    4389                 :            :  * zbookmarks outside of the meta-dnode use their own object and level, and
    4390                 :            :  * calculate the level 0 equivalent (the first L0 blkid that is contained in the
    4391                 :            :  * blocks this bookmark refers to) by multiplying their blkid by their span
    4392                 :            :  * (the number of L0 blocks contained within one block at their level).
    4393                 :            :  * zbookmarks inside the meta-dnode calculate their object equivalent
    4394                 :            :  * (which is L0equiv * dnodes per data block), use 0 for their L0equiv, and use
    4395                 :            :  * level + 1<<31 (any value larger than a level could ever be) for their level.
    4396                 :            :  * This causes them to always compare before a bookmark in their object
    4397                 :            :  * equivalent, compare appropriately to bookmarks in other objects, and to
    4398                 :            :  * compare appropriately to other bookmarks in the meta-dnode.
